Jamison Brereton

20 (461)
Indra
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
13 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except vir─Бj 7
Unlike the usual model, this hymn begins with the prayer for gifts from the god (vs. 1). But most of the rest of the hymn is devoted to a verse-by-verse listing of IndraтАЩs great deeds, not only the standard Vr╠еtra (vs. 2) and Vala (vss. 3тАУ4) tales, but also the defeat of a series of named enemies on behalf of named mortal clients. Some of these stories are familiar (the ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa/Kutsa story, vss. 4тАУ5, and the stealing of NamuciтАЩs head, vs. 6), and some are mentioned much more rarely (e.g., Vetasu and Tuji, vs. 8), with unclear details. Many of these same stories are also treated in VI.26.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra On the metrical irregularities in the hymn, see Oldenberg ZDMG 55.324 and Noten.

рдпрдГ рд░рдпрд┐рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд░реВрдкрдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛ рдмрд▓реЗрди рдкреГрддреНрд╕реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рдЕрд░реНрдпрдГ рдЕрд░реАрдиреН рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЬрдирд╛рдиреН рдЕрднрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдереМ рдЖрдХреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрддреН ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГред рджреНрдпреМрд░реНрди ред рджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛ рдпрдерд╛ рднреВрдо рднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐ рдЖрдХреНрд░рд╛рдорддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН ред рд╣реЗ рд╕рд╣рд╕рдГ рд╕реВрдиреЛ рдмрд▓рд╕реНрдп рдкреБрддреНрд░ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рддрдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдВ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рджрджреНрдзрд┐ рджреЗрд╣рд┐ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдореН ред рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рднрд░рдВ рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рднрд░реНрддрд╛рд░рдореН рдЙрд░реНрд╡рд░рд╛рд╕рд╛рдореН рдЙрд░реНрд╡рд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╕рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рднреВрдореАрдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдирд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╕рдВрднрдХреНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рддреБрд░рдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рддрд░рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡рд╛ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, son of strength, grant us (a son), the possessor of thousands, the owner of cultivated lands, the usbduer of foes, the riches that may overcome men in battles by strength, as the radiant (sun) overspreads the earth by his rays.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Grant us a son: the epithets seem to refer to a son, putram, who is metaphorically the riches of a family, and its defence againstt enemies, putrar┼лpam dhanam yo ┼Ыavas─Б ┼Ыatr┼лn ─Бkramet

Jamison Brereton

O Indra, wealth that in its vast power surmounts (the wealth) of the stranger, (namely) the peoples in battles, as heaven does the earth,
that brings thousands as plunder, wins fertile fields, and overcomes
obstaclesтАФgive that (wealth) to us, o son of strength.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the тАЬaskтАЭ in this hymn comes at the beginning, not the end as is more usual. It is also excessively convoluted in syntax and phraseology. (My interpr. of the vs. is in great part guided by Thieme [Fremdl. 58] and to a certain extent Geldner, though as far as I can see Geldner simply fails to tr. parts of it.) The actual referent of the definitional rel. cl. that occupies the first hemistich is not encountered until the second word of p─Бda b (ray├нс╕е), preceded by a discontinuous simile dya├║r n├б тАж bh┼л╠Бma тАЬlike heaven the earth,тАЭ whose first part has been fronted around the rel. prn. y├бс╕е, and by a verb in tmesis, abh├н тАж tastha├║ тАЬsurmounts,тАЭ whose preverb is stationed after the caesura in p─Бda a and whose verb form proper opens p─Бda b. And this is only the beginning! A first paraphrase of the first hemistich would be тАЬas heaven (surmounts) the earth, the wealth that surmounts тАж,тАЭ with тАЬwealthтАЭ corresponding grammatically and functionally to тАЬheaven.тАЭ This first stab makes it immediately clear that we need an acc. obj. in the frame to correspond to bh┼л╠Бma in the simile, something that wealth can тАЬsurmount.тАЭ One acc. is obvious: j├бn─Бn at the end of the hemistich. But what do we do with ary├бс╕е at the end of the first p─Бda? Oldenberg (ZDMG 54.169-70) takes it as an acc. pl., tr. тАЬwie die Himmel ├╝ber der Erde (sollen) die Sch├дtze ├╝ber den Geizigen (erhaben sein).тАЭ However, there is a reasonably well-attested phrase r─Б╠Бyo ary├бс╕е тАЬthe riches of the strangerтАЭ (IV.48.1, VI.14.3, VI.47.9, and esp. VI.36.5; cf. also VI.1.5 and comm. on all those passages). In VI.36.5 it is found in exactly this context: dya├║r n├б bh┼л╠Бm─Бbh├н r─Б╠Бyo ary├бс╕е тАЬLike heaven over the earth, sur(mount) the riches of the stranger,тАЭ with r─Б╠Бyo ary├бс╕е an object phrase exactly parallel to bh┼л╠Бma in the simile. It therefore seems best here to assume a gapping of acc. pl. r─Б╠Бyaс╕е, whose presence is suggested by the nom. ray├нс╕е, with ary├бс╕е a gen. as elsewhere. Hence тАЬwealth that surmounts (the wealth/riches) of the stranger тАжтАЭ And what does this тАЬwealth of the strangerтАЭ consist of? In all cases it seems to refer to manpower, not to material wealth, and our passage makes this clear by further specifying it as j├бn─Бn тАШpeople(s)тАЩ.

As if the poet hadnтАЩt misled us enough already with the intertwining of constituents and gapping of a crucial word, he also plants a false cue. The word bh┼л╠Бma is of course the acc. sg. to the neut. n-stem bh┼л╠Бman-, as shown esp. by the parallel VI.36.5. But in its position directly after the preverb abh├н, it looks mighty like a verb – and could almost (but only almost) be the 1st pl. root aor. bh┼лma, though with wrong accent (expect *bh┼лm├б, a form not found in the RV). The lexeme abh├н тИЪbh┼л is close in meaning to the abh├н тИЪsth─Б we have here (whose verbal part has been postponed till the 2nd p─Бda), and given its sandhi form the rel. prn. y├б (underlying y├бс╕е) could equally be underlying y├й, which could match the number of the putative 1st pl. verb form (тАЬwe who surmount тАжтАЭ). Of course, as just noted, the accent on bh┼л╠Бma is wrong, and we would further expect abh├н to lose its own accent and univerbate with an immediately following verb in a rel. clause. But I nonetheless think that the poet meant for his audience to follow this false trail, however briefly.

After this tangled beginning, the second hemistich is completely straightforward: the acc. t├бm picks up the rel. cl. couched in the nom., with the implicit referent тАЬwealth,тАЭ modified by three acc. OBJ+VERBAL NOMINAL cmpds, all objects of тАЬgiveтАЭ (daddh├н). This is the last time in the hymn that Indra is asked to give us anything; the only other appeal to Indra is in 10a, where we pray to тАЬwin anew.тАЭ Almost all of the rest of the hymn treats previous heroic deeds of Indra, though it should be noted that many of these are presented in the injunctive, and the notoriously slippery usage of the injunctive may leave the possibility of current application open.

Griffith

GIVE us wealth, Indra, that with might, as heaven o’ertops the earth, o’ercomes our foes in battle
Wealth that brings thousands and that wins the corn-lands, wealth, Son of Strength! that vanquishes the foeman.

Geldner

Den Reichtum, der an Kraft hoch und niedrig in den K├дmpfen ├╝berlegen ist, wie der Himmel ├╝ber die Erde, o Indra, der tausendfachen Gewinn bringt, der Felder erringt und Feinde ├╝berwindet, den gib uns, du Sohn der Kraft!

Grassmann

Den Reichthum, Indra, der die Feind’ in Schlachten mit Kraft umspannt, wie Himmelsrund die Erde, Der Feld uns schafft und tausendfaches Gut bringt, den Feindbezwinger, schenke, Sohn der Kraft, uns.

Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рджрд┐рд╡реЛ рди рджрд┐рд╡реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдпреЗрд╡ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреБрднреНрдпрдВ рд╕рддреНрд░рд╛ рд╕рддреНрдпрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рдЕрд╕реБрд░реНрдпрдореН рдЕрд╕реБрд░рддреНрд╡рдВ рдмрд▓рдВ рджреЗрд╡реЗрднрд┐рдГ рджреЗрд╡реИрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреБ рдзрд╛рдпрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрдзрд╛рдпрд┐ ред рдЕрдХрд╛рд░рд┐ ред рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реИрдГ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рдмрд▓рд╡рддреА рднрд╡рддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╣реЗ рдЛрдЬреАрд╖рд┐рдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЧрддрд░рд╕рд╕реЛрдореЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреБрдирд╛ рд╕рдЪрд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдВрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдореН ред тАШрд╖рдЪ рд╕рдорд╡рд╛рдпреЗ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдзрд╛рддреЛ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдпрддреН рдпреЗрдирд╛рд╕реБрд░реНрдпреЗрдг рдЕрдкрдГ рдЙрджрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╡реНрд░рд┐рд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН рдЕрд╣рд┐рдореН рдЖрдЧрддреНрдп рд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рдореН рдЕрд╕реБрд░рдВ рд╣рдиреН рдЕрд╣рдиреН рдЕрд╡рдзреАрдГ рддрджреНрд╡рд▓рдВ рд╡реНрдпрдзрд╛рдпреАрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдг рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo you, Indra, as to the sun, all strength has verily been given by the gods; so that, drinker of the stale Soma, associated with Viс╣гс╣Зu, you mightiest slay the hostile Ahi obstructing the waters.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Given by the gods: devebhiс╕е = stotс╣Ыbhiс╕е; stotraiс╕е stuyam─Бn─Б devat─Б balavat─л, a deity becomes strong, being praised with praises; the hostile Ahi: ahim vс╣Ыtram = hant─Бram, Vс╣Ыtra, the destroyer Vс╣Ыtra

Jamison Brereton

All lordly power, like (that) of heaven, was entirely ceded to you by the gods, o Indra,
when you, accompanied by Viс╣гс╣Зu, smashed the serpent Vr╠еtra, who had obstructed the waters, you possessor of the silvery drink.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. begins like vs. 1, with a form of тАШheavenтАЩ followed by the simile marker n├б (1a dya├║r n├б, 2a div├│ n├б). In this case there is nothing in the frame that explicitly corresponds to the gen. div├бс╕е in the simile, though the dat. t├║bhyam is roughly parallel: like the тАЬlordship of heaven,тАЭ lordship was conceded to you (Indra) and is therefore yours.

The standard idiom for тАШconcedeтАЩ is ├бnu тИЪd─Б, not, as here, ├бnu тИЪdh─Б. Cf., with phraseology similar to here, VI.25.8 ├бnu te d─Бyi тАж satr─Б╠Бte v├н┼Ыvam тАж (sim.

II.20.8). But тИЪdh─Б is also found in this idiom elsewhere, e.g., VI.36.2 satr─Б╠Бdadhire ├бnu v─лry─Б╠Аya. Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.326, Noten) seems prepared to follow Grassmann (Tr.) and v.

Bradke in emending dh─Бyi to *d─Бyi, but this seems unnec. The two roots are formally very parallel and in many contexts their meanings are barely distinguishable; I see no reason why тИЪdh─Б cannot have acquired this idiomatic meaning with ├бnu in imitation of ├бnu тИЪd─Б. In this particular case ├бnu тИЪdh─Б may have been used in preference to ├бnu тИЪd─Б because of the technical use of anud├йya- in vs. 11 below. See disc. there.

Note that the тАШlordship, lordly powerтАЩ (asury├а-) is in the control of the gods and conceded to Indra, another indication that the later Asura/Deva divide is not present in the core RV. See also VI.36.1 below.

Griffith

Even as the power of Dyaus, to thee, O Indra, all Asura sway was by the Gods entrusted,
When thou, Impetuous! leagued with Visnu, slewest Vrtra the Dragon who enclosed the waters.

Geldner

Dir, Indra, ward die ganze Asuramacht insgesamt gleich der des Himmels von den G├╢ttern zugestanden, als du, Trinker des Trestersafts mit Vishnu verb├╝ndet den Drachen Vritra erschlugst, der die Gew├дsser eingeschlossen hatte.

Grassmann

Dir, wie dem Himmel, r├дumten alle G├╢tter, o Indra, ein die ganze Gottheitsf├╝lle, Als du dem Vritra, der die Wasser einschloss, die Schlang’ erschlugst, o eilender, mit Vischnu.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen Indra, the destroyer, the most mighty, the strongest of the strong, the giver of food, the possessor of vast splendour, received (the thunderbolt), the shatterer of all the cities (of the asuras), he became the lord of the sweet Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Overpowering, mightier and stronger than the strong, he for whom the sacred formulation is created, whose greatness increasedтАФIndra
became king of the somian honey when he aided the splitting of all the strongholds.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation takes Indra as the subj. of ─Б╠Бvat in d, with dartn├║m an action noun тАЬwhen he aided the splitting тАжтАЭ But, on the basis of other -(t)n├║-stems (cf. AiG II.2.696-97 and 741-42), dartn├║- is more likely verbal/agentive (тАШsplitting, splitterтАЩ) and the subject of ─Б╠Бvat should then be soma (тАЬthe somian honeyтАЭ m├бdhu- s├│my├б-).

So explicitly Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.326, with convincing parallels; Geldner appears to follow, though his tr. is more equivocal. I would therefore change the tr. to тАЬwhen it [=soma] aided the splitter of all the strongholds.тАЭ

Griffith

Indra, Strong, Victor, Mightier than the mighty, addressed with prayer and perfect in his splendour,
Lord of the bolt that breaketh forts in pieces, became the King of the sweet juice of Soma..

Geldner

├Ьberwindend als der Kr├дftigere, st├дrker als stark, machterstarkt, wann ihm eine Erbauung bereitet wird, ward Indra K├╢nig des somischen Metes, der dem Brecher aller Burgen half.

Grassmann

Vordringend, st├дrker, m├дchtiger, als Macht ist, voll ausgewachsen Indra durch Gebete, Ward K├╢nig er des s├╝ssen Somatrunkes, als er dem Brecher aller Burgen beistand.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Paс╣Зis, Indra, fled, with hundres (of asuras), from the sage, your worshipper (and ally) in battle; neither did e, (Indra), suffer the deceptions of the powerful ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa to prevail over his weapons, nor did he (leave him) any of his sustenance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

From the sage: da┼Ыoс╣Зaye kavaye = bahu kaviс╣гk─Бt medh─Бvinaс╕е, from the wise man offeing many oblations, that is tvatsah─Бyakuts─Бt, from Kutsa, your ally; elsewhere Da┼Ыoс╣Зi is the name of an asura

Jamison Brereton

The Paс╣Зis were felled here by hundreds (of deadly weapons), o Indra, for the sake of the ten-armed poet at the winning of the (sunтАЩs) rays;
by the deadly weapons the magic powers of the voracious ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa (were felled). Nothing at all had he left over from the meal.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I read the instr. plurals opening the two hemistichs (┼Ыata├нс╕е 4a, vadha├нс╕е 4c) тАЬverticallyтАЭ – that is, as a single NP distributed over two clauses. This seems to be GeldnerтАЩs solution too: тАЬDurch hundert (Streiche) тАж; durch (deine) Streiche тАжтАЭ; so also Oldenberg ZDMG 55.326. The fact that a form of тИЪpad needs to be read in p─Бda c, matching apadran in p─Бda a supports this interpr. It would, however, be possible to interpr. ┼Ыata├нс╕е as тАЬby the hundreds,тАЭ referring to the felled Paс╣Зis. So K├╝mmel (424).

In the published translation I took the beneficiary of IndraтАЩs actions in p─Бda b to be a single person, тАЬthe ten-armed poetтАЭ (d├б┼Ыoс╣Зaye kav├бye)(so Geldner), and since d├б┼Ыoс╣Зi- recurs in 8a apparently qualifying vetas├║-, I considered this to be a reference to this shadowy Vetasu. But I now think this identification is incorrect or at least misleading. When the word kav├н- is found in an Indra / Kutsa / ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa context it always (in my current view) refers to U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya, and I believe that to be the case here тАФ strengthened by the fact that the other two occurrences of ark├б-s─Бti- (I.174.7, VI.26.3) are found with kav├н- in the Kutsa / ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa myth, where the word must surely refer to U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya. (Oldenberg makes the same point, ZDMG 55.326-27.) I therefore now think that тАЬfor the poetтАЭ means тАЬfor U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya,тАЭ and тАЬfor the ten-armedтАЭ is likely a reference to a different person, identified as Vetasu in vs. 8. (Oldenberg considers the additional possibility that d├б┼Ыoс╣Зi- is an epithet of UK, but seems to favor the separation into two individuals.) On the basis of 8a and GeldnerтАЩs disc. there (n. 8), it further seems likely, or at least possible, that vetas├║- in 8 refers to Kutsa, and therefore in our 4b the two datives refer to Kutsa and UK. I would therefore now alter the tr. to тАЬfor the sake of the ten-armed one [=Kutsa?] and of the poet [=U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya].тАЭ My tr. of d├б┼Ыoс╣Зi- in this vs. and in 8a reflects the current consensus, endorsed by Mayr (EWA s.v. oс╣З├н- тАЬoffenbar тАШArmтАЩтАЭ), that oс╣З├н- means тАШarmтАЩ (as opposed to GrassmannтАЩs тАШSchutzтАЩ and тАШMutterbrustтАЩ), but I think that this interpr. might be ripe for revisiting. The passages are not particularly diagnostic – the most important evidence is the fact that the stem is generally dual – and it lacks a clear etymology (though itтАЩs sometimes connected with тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ). There is also the question of the cmpd. sandhi: if d├б┼Ыoс╣Зi- consists of d├б┼Ыa + oс╣З├н-, it should of course come out as

*d├б┼Ыauс╣Зi-. The -o- has been accounted for (see EWA s.v. oс╣З├н- [p.c from J. Schindler], Mayr PN s.v. d├б┼Ыoniya-) by invoking TS I.2.6.1, where the widely attested mantra abh├н ty├бс╣Г dev├бс╣Г savit─Б╠Бram oс╣Зy├▓с╕е kav├нkratum (AV VII.14.1, etc.) instead contains ┼лс╣Зy├▓с╕е. The ┼л- initial would indeed yield the proper sandhi result, but given the otherwise overwhelming attestation of oс╣Зy├▓с╕е in the mantra, the TS variant does not have much support. Since at present I donтАЩt have a better solution, I stick with тАШtenarmedтАЩ, but consider it quite dubious.

That ark├б-s─Бti means тАШwinning of the (sunтАЩs) raysтАЩ is strongly suggested by s┼л╠Бryasya s─Бta├║ in the next vs. (5d), though, as Oldenberg points out (ZDMG 55.327), it could in addition mean тАШwinning of the chantsтАЩ.

I donтАЩt understand p─Бda d, but I would point out that another тАЬinsatiable ┼Ъuс╣гс╣ЗaтАЭ passage also has a mention of mealtime: IV.16.12 k├║ts─Бya ┼Ы├║с╣гс╣Зam a┼Ы├║с╣гaс╣Г n├н barh─лс╕е, prapitv├й ├бhnaс╕е k├║yavaс╣Г sah├бsr─Б тАЬFor Kutsa you laid low insatiable ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa, who brings bad harvest, with his thousands, before the day’s first meal.тАЭ Perhaps the point is that despite his voraciousness, ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa is deprived of his meal by IndraтАЩs timely blow. In that case the subj. of arirec─лt тАж pr├б here is Indra, who leaves nothing for ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa passed away upon the falling of the thunderbolt, then the universal strength of the great oppressor was annihilated, and Indra enlarged their common car for (the use of) his charioteer Kutsa, for (the sake of) the worship of the sn.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

S┼лryasya s─Бtau bh─Бhane nimittabh┼лte; uru с╣гa saratham kar = sam─Бnuratham vistirс╣Зam akarot; Kuts is the reputed author of the hymns to S┼лrya and Uс╣гas: RV. 1.113 and 115

Jamison Brereton

A whole lifetime of great deception was set aside when ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa was felled at the flying of the mace.
Sharing the same chariot, Indra made a wide way for Kutsa, the sharer of his chariot, at the winning of the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the unusual position of s├б and its rukied initial (ur├║ с╣г├б) see disc. ad VI.2.4.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner (n. 4-5) notes, these two vss. probably belong together as an account of the ever-fragmented ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa / Kutsa myth, though the connection of the Paс╣Зis (p─Бda a) to this myth is somewhat uncertain. Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.326-27) treats these vss. in detail.

Griffith

What time the thunder fell and Susna perished, all life’s support from the great Druh was taken.
Indra made room for his car-drivcr Kutsa who sate beside him, when he gained the sunlight.

Geldner

Des gro├Яen Unholdes ganze Lebenszeit war zu Ende, als im Fallen der Keule Susna hinsank. Indra machte auf gleichem Wagen seinem Wagenlenker Kutsa bei der Gewinnung der Sonne freie Bahn.

Grassmann

Des grosen Unholds Leben ward genommen, des ├Зuschna, als durch Blitzes Wurf er hinsank; Raum schaffte Indra Kutsa, dem Gef├дhrten, auf gleichem Wagen, zu des Lichts Erlangung.

English translation:

тАЬAnd the hawk bore to Indra the exhilarating Soma, when, bruising the head of the oppressor Namuci, and protecting the slumbering Nami, the son of Sapya, he provided, for the weeell-being (of the sage), riches and food.тАЭ

Like the falcon stealing the exhilarating plant for him, he, stealing the head of the D─Бsa Namuci,
helped Nam─л S─Бpya as he slept. He imbued (him) with wealth, with
refreshment, and with well-being.

Griffith

As the Hawk rent for him the stalk that gladdens, he wrenched the head from Namuci the Dasa.
He guarded Nam, Sayya’s son, in slumber, and sated him with food, success, and riches.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have scatered by force, wielder of the thunderbolt, the strong cities of the deadly-deluding Pipru; you have given, bountiful Indra, uninjurable wealh to rijiс╣гvat, the donor of sacrificial gifts.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You split open the fortified strongholds of Pipru, who had the tricks of a snake, o mace-bearer, as if with swelling strength.
O generous giver, you gave that legacy not to be spurned as a gift to the pious R╠еji┼Ыvan.

Griffith

Thou, thunder-armed, with thy great might hast shattered Pipru’s strong forts who knew the wiles of serpents.
Thou gavest to thy worshipper Rjisvan imperishable Wealth, O Bounteous Giver.

Geldner

Die festen Burgen des Pipru, der sich in einen Drachen verwandelte, hast du Keulentr├дger wie mit Gewalt zersprengt. Du reichlich Schenkender hast dieses unverge├Яliche Besitztum dem opferspendenden Rijisvan als Geschenk gegeben.

Grassmann

Des schlangelist’gen Pipru feste Burgen zerbrachst du, o gewalt’ger Blitzestr├дger; Vielgebender, du gabst zum Lohn dem frommen Ridschi├зvan diesen Schatz, der unvertilgbar.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, the granter of wished-for felicity, compelled the many-fraudulent Eta┼Ыa and Dasoс╣Зi, T┼лtuji, Tugra and Ibha, always to come submissively to (the r─Бj─Б) Dyotana, as a son (comes before a mother).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra showed the favor of his dominance to Vetasu of the ten tricks and ten arms and to the thrusting (Tuji), (saying,)
тАЬTugra as perpetual vassal for brilliant (Vetasu) shall I dispatch, like (calves) to their mother, to go (to him).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is made difficult both by our very sketchy knowledge of the personnel and the myth and by the syntax. Both Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.328-29) and Geldner (n.

  1. devote considerable space to disc. of it. The vs. seems to pun on PNs in a way discouragingly similar to VII.18, the very obscure account of the Ten Kings battle.

The nearby vs. VI.26.4 is of some help in the interpr. of this one, as is X.49.4.

My approach to the vs. partly follows GeldnerтАЩs, but differs in several important ways. Like Geldner (who adopted it from Baunack; see his n. 8), I supply a verb of speaking to introduce the second hemistich, which we both take as the direct speech of Indra. (By contrast Oldenberg construes ├║pa sс╣Ыj─Б in d as the verb governing the acc. in ab, but given the distribution of the rest of the elements in the vs., esp. the preverb ─Б╠Б opening p─Бda c, this seems unlikely.) But rather than taking the acc. PNs in ab as the addressees of this speech as Geldner does, I construe them (loosely) with the hapax bahuvr─лhi svabhiс╣гс╣н├н-sumnaс╕е тАШhaving/showing the favor of his dominanceтАЩ, with Vetasu [=Kutsa?] and Tuji as the recipient of this favor. The intens. adj. t┼л╠Бtuji- тАШthrustingтАЩ, found elsewhere modifying a whirlwind (bhс╣Ы╠Бmi- IV.32.2) and a chariot (X.35.6), punningly points to Tuji, who is found in nearby VI.26.4 in the company of Vetasu and Tugra, as here. (In that vs. there is also redupl., but it is located on the verb: tv├бс╣Г t├║jim тАж t┼лtoс╕е тАЬyou strengthened Tuji.тАЭ) In that vs. Indra strikes down Tugra for Vetasu (VI.26.4c tv├бс╣Г t├║graс╣Г vetas├бve s├бc─Бhan). I think the same situation is depicted here in cd, though less violently, with Vetasu(-Kutsa) referred to by the adj. dy├│tana- тАШbrilliant, flashingтАЩ expressing a dat. of benefit. In this connection BaunackтАЩs adducing (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 8c) of I.63.3 kuts─Б╠Бya dyumat├й тАЬfor heaven-bright Kutsa,тАЭ another dat. of benefit in the ┼Ъuс╣гс╣Зa myth, is apposite. Geldner (also Grassmann, Mayr PN) takes dy├│tan─Бya as a PN, but no such person Dyotana is found elsewhere, and in its other two occurrences (I.123.4, VIII.29.2) the stem is an adj. with the expected etymological meaning.

The next question is ├нbham. This is pretty much universally interp. as a PN, referring to another enemy of Indra. This is in part based on X.49.4, where Tugra and one Smadibha are made subject to Kutsa (and the Vetasus [pl.] and Tuji are also found). Oldenberg, for ex., considers Ibha here simply a shortening of Smadibha, and the context of the word in our p─Бda certainly supports a pun on the latter name: (─Б╠Б t├║graс╣Г ┼Ы├б)┼Ыvad ├нbham тАж; cf. X.49.4 (t├║graс╣Г k├║ts─Бya) sm├бdibham, with the last syllable of the adverb ┼Ы├б┼Ыvad a close match for the 1st syllable of the PN in X.49.4 (if it is indeed a PN). But ├нbha- is elsewhere in the RV a common noun meaning тАШretinueтАЩ or тАШvassalтАЩ (the common denominator being the inferior position vis-├а-vis someone in power); cf. also the MIA evidence, such as P─Бli ibbha. And тАШvassalтАЩ would be an appropriate word for someone made subject to another – hence my tr. of the phrase ┼Ы├б┼Ыvad ├нbham as тАЬperpetual vassal,тАЭ referring to Tugra.

Finally, we must deal with the verbal expressions at the end of the vs., ├║pa ┼Ыс╣Ыj─Б iy├бdhyai. The first question is what form sс╣Ыj─Б represents out of sandhi. The Pp.

reads sс╣Ыja, that is, a 2nd sg. act. impv., with lengthening of the final vowel in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text. But of course in that case the normal outcome in sandhi should be coalescence into *sс╣Ыjey├бdhyai. After some agonizing, Oldenberg accepts the Pp interpr.

(though he also flirts with a 2nd sg. subj. sс╣Ыj─Бс╕е), but Geldner (n. 8) opts instead for BaunackтАЩs suggestion, that the underlying form is sс╣Ыjai, i.e., a 1st sg. middle subjunctive (so also Lubotsky, though with !). This is the interpr. I have also adopted.

Although the 6th cl. pres. sс╣Ыja- is predominately active, there are a few middle forms; the pf. is about evenly divided between active and middle forms in transitive usage (including several 1st pl. sasс╣Ыjm├бhe with ├║pa), and there are two 1st sg. s-aor. forms ├бsс╣Ыkс╣гi with ├║pa in trans. usage. Taking the form as a 1st sg. also entails the directspeech interpr. of Baunack/Geldner (It’s worth noting as an aside that S─Бyaс╣Зa. simply glosses upa sс╣Ыja with up─Бsс╣Ыjat, apparently untroubled by matters of sandhi and grammatical identity; this was followed by Grassmann [Tr.], though unmentioned in the W├╢.) As Oldenberg points out (ZDMG 55.328), the lexeme ├║pa тИЪsс╣Ыj is often used of releasing / dispatching calves to their mother, and this must account for the simile m─Бt├║r n├б. Although this idiom is generally benevolent, it also emphasizes the hierarchical dependency of the young on their mother, and this would be appropriate for the vassal TugraтАЩs subordinate position with regard to Kutsa.

I take the inf. iy├бdhyai to тИЪi тАШgoтАЩ, or more particularly to the stem ─л╠Бyate тАШspeedsтАЩ (тИЪi or тИЪy─Б), rather than to тИЪy─Б тАШimplore, begтАЩ with Lubotsky It simply completes the action of the main verb тАЬrelease/depatch them to go тАжтАЭ The preverb ─Б╠Бbeginning the 2nd hemistich is more likely to go with this inf. than with ├║pa srjai (pace Grassmann, also Geldner, who thinks [n. 8c] it could go with either one), simply because weтАЩd otherwise expect the order ├║pa+─Б╠Б(cf. VIII.27.11 ├║pa тАж ─Б╠Бm╠Р, ├бsс╣Ыkс╣гi тАж).

After all this, the alterations of the published translation would be minimal: тАЬIndra showed the favor of his dominance to Vetasu [=Kutsa?] of the ten tricks and ten arms and to the thrusting (Tuji), (saying) тАШTugra as perpetual vassal for brilliant (Vetasu=Kutsa?) shall I dispatch, like (calves) to their mother, to speed (to him).тАЩтАЭ

Griffith

The crafty Vetasu, the swift Dasni, and Tugra speedily with all his servants,
Hath Indra, gladdening with strong assistance, forced near as ’twere to glorify the Mother.

Geldner

Zu Vetasu mit zehn Listen, mit zehn Armen, dem Angreifer sprach Indra, dessen Gunst ├Ьberlegenheit gibt: “Den Tugra, den Ibha will ich dem Dyotana zutreiben, da├Я er immer wieder zu ihm komme wie das Kalb zum Euter der Mutter”.

Grassmann

Den sehr gewandten Vetasu, den schnellen Da├зoni und mit allen Dienern Tugra, Dem Djotana entsandt’ sie Indra h├╝lfreich, wie aus der Mutter Schooss zu ihm zu kommen.

Elizarenkova

рдЧрднрд╕реНрддреМ рд╣рд╕реНрддреЗ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рд╡реГрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрдорд╛рдпреБрдзрдВ рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддреН рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреН рдЕрдкреНрд░рддреАрддрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рд░рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдЧрддрдГ рд╕рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕реНрдкреГрдзрдГ рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрдзрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рдИрдореН рдЗрдорд╛рдиреН рд╡реГрддреНрд░рдкреНрд░рднреГрддреАрди рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╡рдирддреЗ рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╣рд░реА рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрд╡реМ рдЕрдзрд┐ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреН рдЖрд░реЛрд╣рддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдЕрд╕реНрддреЗрд╡ рдЧрд░реНрддреЗ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкреНрддрд╛ рд╢реВрд░реЛ рд░рдереЗрд╜рдзрд┐рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН ред рддрдерд╛ рд╡рдЪреЛрдпреБрдЬрд╛ рд╡рдЪреЛрдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдг рдпреБрдЬреНрдпрдорд╛рдиреМ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдпреБрдЬреНрдпрдорд╛рдиреМ рддреМ рд╣рд░реА рдЪ рдЛрд╖реНрд╡рдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдВ рд╡рд╣рддрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBearing in his hand the foe-destroyig thunderbolt, Indra, unresisted, demolishing those his adversaries; he mounts his two-horse (car), as a warrior (ascends) his chariot; harnessed at a word, his steeds, convey the migty Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Unopposable, he will vanquish the contenders, bearing his
Vr╠еtra-smashing mace in his fist.
He mounts his two fallow bays, like an archer upon his chariot seat; those yoked by speech convey lofty Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The participial phrase b├нbhrad v├бjram here and in VI.23.1 below may be intended to invoke the name bhar├бd-v─Бja-, the poet of this hymn and indeed of this maс╣Зс╕Нala, by an expression that seems the syntactic equivalent of that type of governing compound тАФ with the prior member belonging to the same root and the 2nd member a phonological variant of the obj. Matching the first member exactly would be problematic, since the nom. sg. of the participle would be bh├бran. The punning on PNs noted with regard to the immediately preceding vs. may be in evidence here as well.n

Griffith

Resistless, with the hosts he battles, bearing in both his arms the Vrtra-slaying thunder.
He mounts his Bays, as the car-seat an archer: yoked at a word they bear the lofty Indra.

Geldner

Er ├╝berwindet unwiderstehlich die Gegner, der die vritrat├╢tende Keule in der Hand tr├дgt. Er besteigt die Hari┬┤s wie ein Sch├╝tze den Sch├╝tzenstand. Die auf blo├Яes Wort Geschirrten fahren den hohen Indra.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Favoured) by your proection, Indra, we solicit new (wealth); by this adoration men glorify you at sacrifices, for that you have shattered with your bolt the seven cities of ┼Ъarat, killing the opponents (of sacred rites), killing the opponents (of sacred rites), and giving (their spoils) to Purukutsa.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Men: puravaс╕е = manuс╣гyaс╕е;

┼Ъarat = name of an asura

Jamison Brereton

Might we win anew through your help, Indra. The P┼лrus start up the praise with this (hymn) along with sacrifices.
When he split the seven autumnal strongholds, their shelter, he smote the D─Бsa (clans), doing his best for Purukutsa.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b en─Б╠Бcan simply be adverbial, as Geldner and Hoffmann (Injunk. 168) take it, but it is also regularly used as demonstrative with forms like n├бmas─Б тАШhomageтАЩ (I.171.1, II.23.14, etc.), s┼лkt├йna тАШhymnтАЩ (II.6.2), br├бhmaс╣З─Б (IV.36.7), and in this context, where the sacrifice is mentioned (yaj├▒a├нс╕е), I think it likely that the verbal part of the ritual evidenced by the verb pr├б тАж stavante тАЬthey start up the praiseтАЭ is further specified with the near deictic, referring to this current praise hymn.

The syntactic relationship between p─Бdas c and d is ambiguous. With Geldner, I take d as the main cl., with c dependent on it. But Hoffmann (Injunk. 168) takes them as parallel subordinate clauses dependent on b. Either is possible, because the verb of d, (d)h├бn, is initial in the p─Бda and can owe its accent to that alone.

Note the allit. in (┼Ы─Б╠Бra)d─лr d├бrd, dh├бn d─Б╠Бs(─лс╕е), esp. noticeable because it consists of four syllables in a row, belonging to four separate words.

Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.329-30 and Noten) calls dart in c into question, arguing that it should be a 2nd ps. and the -t is faulty. But there seems no reason not to assume that both dart and (d)han are 3rd ps. verbs; although Indra is referred to in the 2nd ps. in p─Бda a, shift between the persons is a commonplace in RVic discourse. The sandhi situation here favors the retention of the -t, though the matter is somewhat complex.

As is generally known, final clusters are simplified, retaining only the first. The exception is that -t, -с╣н, and -k after -r- are retained if they belong to the root (Wh, Grassmann

┬з150b Macdonell VGS ┬з28a, etc.) – which the -t in dar-t does not (тИЪdс╣Ы). However, dart is p─Бda-final and the next p─Бda begins in the transmitted text with dh├бn (for h├бn), whose dh is the automatic result of the (re-)introduction of occlusion of initial hafter a final stop (see, e.g., Wh, Grassmann ┬з163). The standard practice is that the h- is replaced by the voiced aspirate corresponding to the place of articulartion of the final stop – in this case, a dental. If we assume that this rule was operative before final clusters were simplified, a sequence of 3rd sg. dard dh├бn with apparently pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ gemination would favor the non-simplification of the cluster -rd dh-. (On cases of gemination and degemination in the text, see my тАЬFalse Segmentations and Resegmentations in the Rigveda: Gemination and DegeminationтАЭ [to appear in a forthcoming Fs.].) P─Бda c is identical to I.174.2b, and in that passage the case is more difficult because there the context is entirely 2nd ps. As I argued in the comm. to that vs. (q.v.), the final -t there may have been introduced from our passage.

Griffith

May we, O Indra, gain by thy new favour: so Parus laud thee, with their sacrifices,
That thou hast wrecked seven autumn forts, their shelter, slain Dasa tribes and aided Purukutsa.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDesirous of opulence, you, Indra, have been an ancient benefactor of U┼Ыanas, the son of Kavi; having slain Navav─Бstva, you have given back his own grandson, who was (fit) to be restored o the grandfather.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Indra, became the first strengthener. Making wide space for U┼Ыan─Б K─Бvya,
(to him as?) grandfather you handed over Navav─Бstu, who was to be delivered up, as his own grandson.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c contains one of the three instances of the gerundive anud├йya- in the RV and the only masc. form – a form called by Geldner тАЬganz unsicher.тАЭ This gerundive belongs to the lexeme ├бnu тИЪd─Б тАШhand over, concedeтАЩ discussed above, ad vs. 2. I have discussed one of the fem. forms anud├йy─л in the difficult hymn X.135 at length (тАЬThe Earliest Evidence for the Inborn Debts of a Brahmin: A New Interpretation of с╣Ъgveda X.135.тАЭ Journal asiatique 302.2 [2014]: 245-57). In that article I established that the idiom ├бnu тИЪd─Б can be further narrowed in certain contexts to mean тАШforgive/acquit a debtтАЩ; and the debt in question can be referred to with the gerund anud├йya-, -─л, as (the debt) тАШto be acquitedтАЩ. In X.135.5-6 this debt is actually a reference to the inborn debts of a Brahman, which he must pay off during his lifetime, one of which is the need to provide his ancestors with (grand)sons. As argued in that article (255-56), I think the same sense can be seen in our passage. To cite from the article: тАЬThe second half of this verse seems to allude to a complex intergenerational relationship in which Indra intervenes. The god hands over a grandson (n├бp─Бt-) to his grandfather (mah├й pitr├й), a transaction that sounds like a man’s fulfillment of his debt to his ancestors by fathering a son, thereby providing them with a grandson. This grandson is said to be anud├йya-. I would suggest that the grandson here serves as the concrete manifestation of the debt that is to be acquitted, and the technical term anud├йya- is therefore applied to him. If I am correct, this is another, though more muted, piece of evidence for the existence of the notion of a man’s inborn debt in the Rig Veda.тАЭ

Griffith

Favouring Usana the son of Kavi, thou wast his ancient strengthener, O Indra.
Thou gavest Navavastva. as a present, to the great father gavest back his grandson.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Indra, who make (your enemies) tremble, have caused the waters, detained by Dhuni, to flow like rushing rivers; so, hero, when, having crossed the ocean, you have reached the shore, you have brought over in safety Turva┼Ыa and Yadu.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Samudram atipraparс╣гi = samudram atikramya pratirс╣Зo bhavasi = when you are crossed, having traversed the ocean, you have brought across Turva┼Ыa and Yadu, both standing on the future shore, samudrap─Бre tiс╣гс╣нhantau ap─Бrayaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

You, the tumultuous one, Indra, set the tumultuous waters in motion, flowing like streams.
When you will cross the sea, o hero, make Turva┼Ыa and Yadu cross to well-being.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is identical to I.174.9; see comm. on that vs., esp. with regard to p├бrс╣гi.

Griffith

Thou, roaring Indra, drovest on the waters that made a roaring sound like rushing rivers,
What time, O Hero, o’er the sea thou broughtest, in safety broughtest Turvasa and Yadu.

Geldner

Du, Indra, der Tosende, setztest die tosenden Gew├дsser in Bewegung, die str├╢men, wie die Fl├╝sse gew├╢hnt sind. Wenn du ├╝ber das Meer fahren kannst, o Held, so fahre den Turvasa und Yadu heil hin├╝ber !

Grassmann

Die brausenden Gew├дsser liessest rauschend du, Indra, rinnen, die wie Str├╢me flossen; Wie du zum Meer, o Held, hindurch sie leitest, so f├╝hr zum Heile Turva├зa und Jadu.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAll this, Indra, has been your work in war; you have put to sleep, (in depth), the slumbering Dhun─л and Cumur─л; and thereupon Dabh─лti, pouring the libation, preparing the oblation, and supplying the fuel, has glorified you with Soma offerings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Everything in the contest is yours, Indra. Dhuni and Cumuri sleep, whom you put to sleep.
Just he will shine: Dabh─лti who presses for you with the soma juices, who brings the firewood and the cooked food, along with the chants.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Dabh─лti is the beneficiary of IndraтАЩs putting Cumuri to sleep in VI.26.6.

CumuriтАЩs companion Dhuni is found with him in VI.18.8, and in our passage he immediately follows vs. 12, which contains two adj. usages of dh├║ni- тАШtumultuous, boisterousтАЩ.

The second hemistich portrays Dabh─лti assembling or preparing four different requisites of the sacrifice in four different morphosyntactic expressions: 1) a full participial phrase s├│mebhiс╕е sunv├бn тАЬpressing with the soma juices,тАЭ 2) a bahuvr─лhi idhm├бbhс╣Ыtiс╕е lit. тАШhaving the bringing of the firewoodтАЩ, 3) an -├нn-stem possessive pakth─л╠БтАШhaving cooked foodтАЩ (based on an unattested *pakth├б- тАШcooked foodтАЩ), and 4) an instr. of accompaniment arka├нс╕е тАЬalong with the chants.тАЭ The identity of the third has been called into question by Oldenberg (ZDMG 55.330, Noten). Though the sandhi form pakthy is analyzed by the Pp. as pakth─л╠Бwith the long vowel appropriate to the nom. sg. of an -├нn-stem, in fact in the cadence it would better be read short (though keep in mind the metrical disturbances throughout the hymn). Oldenberg toys with the idea that it has been influenced by the PN pakth├б- and that it is underlyingly an instr. to the -ti-stem pakt├н- тАШcooked foodтАЩ, hence *pakt─л╠Бwith shortening before the following vowel. This seems unnecessarily complex, and the PN pakth├б- is neither well attested nor found nearby this passage. Since shortening of -─л╠Бin hiatus was available for the instr., I see no reason why it shouldnтАЩt have been analogically extended to the nom. of an -├нn-stem in this case. Moreover, I think the morphosyntactic variety just described was deliberate, and replacing 3) with an instr. like that of 4) would disturb the sequence.

Griffith

This Indra, was thy work in war: thou sentest Dhuni and Cumuri to sleep and slumber.
Dabhiti lit the flame for thee, and worshipped with fuel, hymns, poured Soma, dressed oblations.

Grassmann

Dies ganze Werk ist, Indra, dein im Kampfe; Dhuni und Tschumuri, durch dich sind sie entschlafen; Da gl├дnzte dir mit Liedern, Somatr├дnken Dabhiti pressend, Brennholz schichtend, kochend.

Elizarenkova
